(2) Entity-based indexing for retrieval — recurring concepts as first-class entities that bridge different structural contexts, adapted as a future retrieval signal for cross-project knowledge alongside section-type-based structural matching. Implementation rejected: Rust single-file memory layer introduces a compiled dependency and different runtime model. fctry's memory store remains a plain markdown file with agent-driven operations.

- **roborev** (https://github.com/roborev-dev/roborev) — A local daemon and CLI for continuous automated code review of AI coding agent output. Its closed review-fix-review loop (`refine` command: review finds issues, fix addresses them with directed guidance, re-review verifies and surfaces remaining issues — structurally different from blind retry), post-completion consolidation (`compact` command: re-verifies all open findings against current codebase, filters false positives from issues fixed since the review, consolidates related findings), and project-scoped review guidelines (explicit "this is NOT a finding" declarations injected into every review prompt, preventing predictable false positives) informed fctry's Observer behavioral review tier with directed fix guidance, build-level finding consolidation pass, and project-scoped verification guidelines. Its isolated worktree pattern for background fix jobs (never modifying the user's working tree — fixes run in isolated git worktrees, patches applied only on explicit confirmation) was noted as relevant to fctry's future background-worker execution direction. Its context-check-before-CLI-call pattern (checking conversation context before fetching via CLI to avoid redundant tool calls) was noted as a minor agent workflow refinement.

- **Attractor** (https://github.com/strongdm/attractor) — Three NLSpec documents specifying StrongDM's software factory pipeline runner — a DOT-graph-based pipeline orchestrator where directed graphs describe multi-stage AI workflows. The repo is specs, not code — validating fctry's core thesis that specifications drive implementation. Its declarative context fidelity modes (six graduated levels from `full` session reuse to `truncate` fresh start, resolved per-edge/per-node/per-graph with explicit precedence) informed fctry's context management evolution from reactive budget gating toward declarative per-chunk fidelity. Its fidelity degradation on resume (when a crashed session resumes, the first node degrades from `full` to `summary:high` because in-memory sessions cannot be serialized, then allows `full` again) directly informed fctry's checkpoint/resume fidelity specification. Its goal gate enforcement (critical nodes marked `goal_gate=true` that must succeed before the pipeline can exit, with retry-target routing on failure) informed fctry's goal-gate chunk pattern — structural quality enforcement at the plan level complementing instruction-level anti-rationalization. Its structured guard evaluation (manager loop handler running observe/guard/steer cycles with explicit continue/intervene/escalate routing) informed fctry's inter-chunk guard evaluation step. Its typed event taxonomy (pipeline/stage/parallel/human/checkpoint event categories with SSE streaming) informed fctry's interview lifecycle and checkpoint-saved events. Its DOT-as-workflow-DSL and CSS-like model stylesheet were noted but rejected — fctry's 3-8 chunk plans don't need a full graph DSL, and model assignment is handled by agent frontmatter.

- **Agate** (https://github.com/strongdm/agate) — A Go CLI that orchestrates AI coding agents through a goal-to-working-software lifecycle: interview, design, sprint planning, implementation with review gates, retrospectives with skill evolution. Its sprint retrospective with skill auto-patching (the `_retro` skill analyzes sprint logs, emits structured `SKILL_UPDATE` blocks, and `applySkillUpdate()` appends versioned improvement sections directly to skill markdown files — learnings become instructions rather than passive context) informed fctry's future direction for lesson-to-instruction graduation. Its four-stage failure escalation (retry → recover → restructure → escalate, with failure history preserved across replans via `MergeFailureCounts()`) sharpened fctry's retry/rearchitect progression with explicit stage naming and the recovery-before-retry concept (fixing environment issues as a distinct step from retrying the task). Its filesystem-derived state via pure function over `fs.FS` was noted but rejected — fctry's `state.json` carries richer state than file existence can express — though the testability pattern (state derivation as a pure function) was noted. Its exit code protocol (0=done, 1=continue, 2=error, 255=human-needed) was noted as a composability pattern that doesn't apply to fctry's plugin architecture.

- **AttractorBench** (https://github.com/strongdm/attractorbench) — StrongDM's benchmark for measuring how well coding agents implement systems from NLSpecs. Its per-section DoD dimensional breakdown (decomposing scores into per-section pass rates rather than a single composite number, enabling diagnosis of "where did the agent fail?") informed fctry's per-section satisfaction decomposition in experience reports. Its cost-per-compliance metrics (tokens-per-point, cost-per-point, compliance efficiency with cache-aware token accounting) informed fctry's build economics tracking in experience reports and build traces. Its run-to-run variability data (same model scoring 0.25 to 0.81 across runs) informed fctry's evaluation variance acknowledgment — treating scenario satisfaction as a trend rather than a precise measurement. Its DoD-as-conformance pattern (parsing spec checklists to generate verification targets) was noted but rejected — fctry's experience-language specs deliberately avoid implementation checklists. Its deterministic mock verification was rejected — fctry verifies real built artifacts, not test doubles.

- **SLANG** (https://github.com/riktar/slang) — A declarative meta-language for multi-agent orchestration ("the SQL of AI agents") built on three primitives: stake (produce and route output), await (block until a dependency resolves), and commit (accept result and terminate the step). Its three-primitive workflow vocabulary validates fctry's agent handoff model — produce-route, block-on-dependency, accept-terminate map cleanly to State Owner briefing, agent prerequisite checking, and step completion with output persistence. Its declarative budget constraints (token and cost limits visible at the flow definition level, not buried in runtime config) reinforce fctry's context budget gate pattern where budget awareness is a first-class execution concern. Its escalate operation as a named first-class primitive — distinct from error handling, explicitly meaning "this exceeds my authority, route to a higher agent" — maps to fctry's experience questions, validating the pattern with sharper vocabulary. Its checkpoint/resume as a core concern (per-round serializable state enabling crash recovery and workflow inspection) validates fctry's per-chunk build checkpoint at a finer granularity. Its workflow-as-documentation principle (the `.slang` file is simultaneously the workflow definition, the execution plan, and the human-readable documentation) aligns with fctry's spec-as-contract philosophy where the spec is both the description and the build instruction.

- **agent-factory** (https://github.com/Dominien/agent-factory) — An autonomous system that discovers problems, scores them, builds AI agents, validates, and ships overnight. Claude Code in headless mode, controlled by a single `program.md` strategy file. Its threshold ratchet pattern — a monotonically increasing quality bar where each shipped agent's score becomes the new floor, forcing progressively better work — validates the direction of fctry's scenario satisfaction as a rising bar (once satisfied, a scenario stays the standard). Its strategy-as-document model (a single markdown file encoding judgment heuristics, scoring formulas, thresholds, and anti-patterns alongside process) validates fctry's spec-as-contract philosophy where one document is both the vision and the build instruction. Its research-as-product principle — accumulated analysis is an asset independent of what gets built, with even rejected ideas logged — aligns with fctry's changelog and lessons as cumulative institutional knowledge. Its context-limit auto-restart with handoff notes validates fctry's checkpoint/resume design for context exhaustion recovery. Its ship-imperfect principle (working beats perfect, document limitations, move on) validates fctry's convergence-over-perfection philosophy.

- **greppy** (https://github.com/wonyoung-jang/greppy) — A daemon-based codebase search engine combining BM25 full-text search with tree-sitter AST parsing, call graph tracing, and impact analysis — all queries sub-millisecond once the daemon is warm. Concrete token benchmarks: 93-98% reduction vs. raw grep/find patterns for equivalent codebase understanding tasks. Its composable multi-analysis operations (chaining symbol lookup → call graph → impact trace in a single query pipeline) informed fctry's composable trace operations concept for the Executor's codebase orientation. Its concrete token savings benchmarks (93-98% reduction with methodology) informed the quantified token savings range in `#capabilities` 3.1, strengthening the context budget case for codebase indexing tools. Its tool dependency model (daemon-based with warm/cold query distinction) informed the codebase indexing tool category in `references/tool-dependencies.md`.

- **sentrux** (https://github.com/sentrux/sentrux) — A Rust-based architecture quality governance tool for AI-assisted development. Session-scoped structural regression gating, 14-dimension A-F health grading with anti-gaming composite scoring (floor-mean capped by worst dimension), live interactive treemap visualization with activity heat, and MCP integration for tool-available environments. Its thesis — the "governor gap" (AI generates code faster than humans can govern architecture) — identifies the exact failure mode fctry's behavioral review misses: code that satisfies scenarios while degrading maintainability. fctry governs the experience (spec + scenarios); sentrux governs the architecture (structural metrics). Neither alone catches both failure modes. Its activity heat treemap (warm colors for active modification, exponential decay for recently completed work) inspired the activity heat visualization in mission control's story map. Its anti-gaming composite grading (no single weak dimension can hide behind strong averages) informed the structural regression dimension for Observer verification.

- **Symphony** (https://github.com/openai/symphony) — OpenAI's spec-first autonomous coding orchestrator that polls a Linear task board, spawns isolated agent workers with persistent workspaces, manages retries with reconciliation, collects proof of work, and lands PRs. Different abstraction level (team-scale ticket-driven vs. fctry's single-user spec-driven), but six transferable patterns: workspace reuse across runs (same issue gets the same workspace, preserving prior artifacts), lightweight turn continuation within workers, formalized trust boundary documentation with layered hardening, reconciliation stop gates that kill workers whose tasks went terminal, conformance test profiles with three verification tiers (core, extension, real-integration), and per-workspace typed lifecycle hooks with timeout enforcement. These patterns reinforce existing fctry concepts (build trace as resumption contract, context-carrying chunks, first-run credential safety, build steering, Observer verification, lifecycle events) and sharpen them with industry-validated specificity.

- **devteam** (https://github.com/agent-era/devteam) — A terminal UI for parallel coding agents in tmux sessions with git worktree isolation. Its priority-cascade status derivation for entity cards (each card highlights the most actionable dimension from a priority waterfall — building > drift > untracked changes > inbox > readiness — rather than showing all status dimensions equally) and implicit urgency sorting within columns (items needing attention float to the top without requiring a filter mode) informed fctry's kanban card status model and within-column sort order.

- **ccpm** (https://github.com/automazeio/ccpm) — A Claude Code plugin using GitHub Issues + git worktrees for parallel agent execution. Confirmatory reference — independently validates fctry's existing worktree isolation, structured callback queuing, and per-chunk file manifest patterns.

- **agent-pm** (https://github.com/gannonh/agent-pm) — An MCP server for AI-assisted project planning with interview-driven briefs and dependency-aware task scheduling. Confirmatory reference — fctry's interview pipeline, dependency ordering, and dual-format artifacts (markdown spec + derived SQLite cache) are already more sophisticated.

- **agentops** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Build learnings feedback loop patterns. Mandatory post-build retro as a lifecycle phase (not optional agent responsibility), utility feedback on lessons (helpful_count/harmful_count tracking when lessons are cited during builds), and bidirectional maturity transitions (prevention ratchet — lessons can be demoted to anti-pattern status when consistently harmful, not just promoted). These patterns address the weakest area in fctry's build-to-build learning loop: lessons were accumulated but never evaluated for actual utility, and harmful lessons could persist indefinitely once they reached active status.

- **opik** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Scenario evaluation mechanism patterns. Multi-trial evaluation (N trials with M/N majority-vote pass criteria to absorb LLM-as-judge noise), scoring failure distinction ("couldn't evaluate" ≠ "not satisfied" — infrastructure failures excluded from satisfaction counts), selective per-chunk evaluation (only scenarios mapped to affected sections), and evaluation as infrastructure (dedicated subsystem with failure isolation, not inline State Owner work). These patterns operationalize fctry's existing variance acknowledgment philosophy with concrete evaluation mechanics.

- **Vibetape** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Memory system denoising and structured lesson patterns. Factor decomposition for memory ranking (recording why each entry was selected for debuggability), denoising rules (unconfirmed lessons decay, near-duplicates consolidate, rewritten-section lessons prune), structured lesson format (rule + supporting evidence + anti-pattern instead of free-form text), and agent provenance on memory entries (originating agent name for filtering and audit). These patterns address memory quality degradation — without denoising, the lessons file accumulates noise that dilutes the signal.

- **ooda-subagents** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Observer verification strengthening patterns from the OODA loop model. Collect-then-judge protocol (complete all evidence collection before rendering any verdict — prevents selective evidence termination), absence checking (verify completeness against spec claims, not just correctness — catches silent omissions), and guard evaluation orientation persistence (the guard writes what was learned from each chunk to the build trace so subsequent chunks benefit from accumulated discoveries). These patterns close verification gaps where the Observer could pass code that was correct but incomplete, or stop collecting evidence once a pass looked likely.

- **hermes-agent-self-evolution** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Feedback loop strengthening patterns. Causal trace analysis (retro extracts WHY-chains from build traces — root cause, not just symptom), growth caps on lessons file (hard ceiling with bidirectional maturity as primary enforcement), per-context lesson ranking (lessons carry per-section-category and per-project-type relevance rather than global utility alone), and scenario source stratification (hand-crafted, spec-derived, and trace-mined scenarios as distinct source types with hand-crafted as the evaluation standard). These patterns address a feedback loop gap: lessons captured outcomes without causal reasoning, ranking was context-blind, and scenarios had no systematic way to grow from build failures.

- **claude-code-hooks-multi-agent-observability** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Hook-sourced telemetry and event infrastructure patterns. PostToolUse hooks as lightweight event emitters (tool-call-level granularity in the activity feed without agent instruction changes), SQLite event persistence (durable cross-session build history alongside the spec index), and request-state WebSocket handshake (eliminating blank-screen-on-connect race conditions). These patterns fill an observability gap between agent-level lifecycle events (coarse) and raw file-watcher updates (noisy).

- **FlowBoard** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Kanban interactivity patterns. Diff-based board rendering (build skeleton once, update cards in-place via DOM diffing), interaction guard (suppress re-renders during drag and input, batch deferred updates), optimistic drag-and-drop with rollback (immediate local state update, server confirmation, revert with toast on failure), and wake events on drag (dragging to "Now" queues an execute action). These patterns address the gap between a kanban board that displays state and one that drives action.

- **claude-dispatcher** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Mission control event delivery patterns. POST-as-canonical-broadcast (single broadcast trigger via HTTP POST, state.json as persistence-only fallback — simplifying dual-path delivery), color-coded event timeline (events carry type-to-color mapping using agent frontmatter colors), chunk health classification (healthy/stalled/context-exhausted as diagnostic indicators on the DAG), and connection status indicator (pulsing dot showing WebSocket health). These patterns improve mission control's information density and reliability.

- **trycycle** (https://github.com/danshapiro/trycycle) — An autonomous coding agent orchestration framework built around a try-verify-fix cycle with structured build phases. Its fresh-agent build-completion audit (a subagent with no build context reads the full diff against the spec after all chunks complete — fresh perspective catches what accumulated-context verification misses), convergence-failure diagnosis (a diagnostic pass producing a root-cause hypothesis before escalation routing — spec ambiguity, architectural mismatch, missing dependency, or environment issue — adding causal precision beyond stagnation pattern detection), independent plan validation (a fresh agent reviews the approved plan against the spec for gaps before execution begins — catching plan-level issues cheaply before they become mid-build problems), and phase-boundary hygiene gates (lightweight ground-truth verification at each phase boundary — git status, checkpoint consistency, spec stability — complementing the guard evaluation's progress quality assessment with state consistency verification) informed fctry's build verification layering, escalation routing precision, plan quality assurance, and state consistency discipline.

- **gru-ai** (https://github.com/andrew-yangy/gru-ai) — A CLI framework for AI-assisted development with a C-suite agent hierarchy (CEO/CTO/developer agents) orchestrated by a "foreman" scheduler that launches autonomous work from cron/launchd. One pattern adopted: foreman scheduler for unattended inbox processing — a scheduled daemon that checks for pending work and triggers processing when capacity, budget, and quiet-hours conditions are met, extending fctry's "factory never idles" invariant from session-scoped to continuous (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1 as a future direction). Its C-suite agent hierarchy and 15-step pipeline are interesting but well-covered by fctry's existing eight-agent architecture with role-based authority and workflow enforcement.

- **agentsview** (https://github.com/wesm/agentsview) — A local-first AI coding agent session analytics dashboard. Six patterns adopted: (1) build autonomy distribution — per-build metric showing agent-initiated vs. human-initiated action percentages, quantifying the "plan-gated then hands-off" experience (adopted into `#observability` 6.3), (2) chunk throughput metrics — time/tool-calls/sections per chunk broken down by complexity, filling fctry's velocity gap alongside existing quality observability (adopted into `#observability` 6.3), (3) session resume from viewer — terminal detection and `claude --resume` launch from the browser UI, a concrete viewer-as-control-plane step (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9), (4) dual-fallback event reliability — file watcher primary with periodic mtime secondary, ensuring the viewer never silently goes stale (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9), (5) persisted narrative insights — post-build LLM-generated retrospective stored as a first-class entity alongside the build trace (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9), (6) spec minimap — condensed structural overview showing section boundaries, readiness heat, and build activity as a navigable sidebar strip (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9).

- **speclock** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Constraint erosion detection patterns. Surfaces when hard constraints are being repeatedly worked around across builds and evolves, turning implicit constraint fatigue into an explicit signal before a constraint is silently abandoned (adopted into `#rules` 3.3).

- **sem** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Entity-level codebase analysis patterns. Entity-level change summaries (function/class-level diffs produce 2.3x higher agent accuracy vs. raw file diffs), structural-vs-cosmetic change distinction for scope compliance, and entity-level impact awareness for chunk sizing (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#capabilities` 3.1).

- **hive** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Escalation and loop detection patterns. Structured escalation tickets (severity/cause/evidence/action rendered as dismissable viewer cards), doom-loop detection (tool-call-level spinning complement to build-level stagnation patterns), and episodic session journals as a future direction for richer cross-session continuity (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#spec-viewer` 2.9).

- **rampart** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Safety refinement patterns. Response-scanning gap awareness (credentials can appear at allowed paths, not just denied ones — path deny + response-level detection are complementary layers) and safety preflight at plan approval (verify deny rules are actually in place before granting autonomous execution authority). Adopted into `#hard-constraints` 4.4 and `#execute-flow` 2.7.

- **claude-octopus** (internal assessment, 2026-03-14) — Compaction survival patterns. PreCompact workflow state snapshot (structured state preservation before compaction fires — complementing the existing PostCompact hook for non-build workflows) and SessionStart invariant reinforcement (re-injecting critical invariants via additionalContext to guarantee survival across compaction and session boundaries). Adopted into `#details` 2.11.

### 5.2 Experience References {#experience-references}

**CXDB — Mission control enrichments, quest lifecycle, and build steering** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-16; enriched 2026-03-11). Source: https://github.com/strongdm/cxdb. The cxdb design discussion of what agentic workloads need from context stores — immutable action tracking, branching on retry, typed events, and run-level provenance — inspired four patterns adopted into fctry's build experience: (1) explicit chunk lifecycle states visible in mission control (planned, active, retrying, completed, failed), (2) retry visibility showing attempt counts instead of invisible retries, (3) typed activity events in the mission control feed (agent started section, chunk retrying, scenario evaluated) replacing generic file-change notifications, and (4) the build run as a first-class entity connecting the approved plan to live progress and the experience report. A second pass (2026-03-11) examined the quest orchestration model visible in the frontend and the design discussion document. Two additional patterns adopted: (5) structured evidence on Observer verification — verdicts carry action summaries, affected files, and spec citations alongside pass/fail, making the build trace more useful for debugging (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7), and (6) confidence indicators on Observer verdicts — high/medium/low based on verification depth achieved (structural vs. behavioral), informing the Executor's retry/continue decision (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). The quest model's typed steering events (sync questions, async input, lifecycle control) informed the unification of fctry's three build steering mechanisms under a single concept (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). Clarification: cxdb is context infrastructure (persistence layer); Attractor is StrongDM's closed-source orchestration engine.

**Leash — Event streaming, drift severity, and spec suggestions** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-16). Source: https://github.com/strongdm/leash. Leash's agent governance architecture — typed event streaming with ring buffers and sequence numbers, a policy suggestion engine that mines observed behavior to propose specific rules, and a three-mode progression (observe, shadow, enforce) — inspired seven patterns adopted into fctry: (1) event history on reconnect so users joining a build mid-progress see everything that's happened, (2) activity feed filtering by event type to manage noise during parallel builds, (3) drift severity assessment that makes the system's response proportional to divergence magnitude, (4) external tool call visibility in mission control (MCP tool invocations as typed events), (5) build log export for post-build review and sharing, (6) the observe-evolve-build progression made explicit in the review flow, and (7) spec update suggestions generated from observed code changes rather than generic drift flags.

**Attractor — Build pipeline patterns** (via `/fctry:evolve`, 2026-02-17). Source: https://github.com/strongdm/attractor. Attractor's DOT-based pipeline orchestration architecture — explicit dependency graphs, checkpoint-and-resume after each pipeline stage, context fidelity modes across stages, a manager loop pattern that monitors and rebalances child pipelines, goal gates as must-succeed checkpoints, and configurable join/error policies for parallel branches — inspired six patterns adopted into fctry: (1) build checkpoint and resume so interrupted builds survive session death and pick up where they left off, (2) a visual dependency graph in mission control rendering the build plan as an interactive DAG with lifecycle-state animations, (3) context fidelity as an autonomous Executor decision guided by execution priorities, (4) build coordination where the Executor monitors overall build health and rebalances work across the dependency graph, (5) convergence milestones as non-blocking validation points at phase boundaries, and (6) execution-priority-driven failure behavior (speed-first = best-effort, reliability-first = fail-fast).

**Claude Context OS — Session resilience and uncertainty tracking** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-17). Source: https://github.com/Arkya-AI/claude-context-os. A CLAUDE.md-only system (no runtime code) for preventing context loss across multi-session Claude work. Its structured session handoff pattern, explicit uncertainty markers, and "write to disk, not conversation" discipline — informed by 9 peer-reviewed papers on how LLMs process system prompts — inspired three refinements adopted into fctry: (1) OPEN/ASSUMED/MISSING uncertainty markers in interview state so paused interviews preserve what's settled vs. what's ambiguous, (2) intermediate agent output persistence to the state file during spec evolution workflows (init, evolve, ref) so that mid-workflow context compaction doesn't lose the State Owner's briefing or the Interviewer's captured answers, and (3) a relevance manifest in the State Owner's briefing — a scoped list of files and sections that matter for the current command — so that session resumption and subsequent agents can load targeted context rather than scanning everything. Also validated fctry's existing progressive disclosure architecture (hub-and-spoke matches their 7-rule cap finding from working memory research), disk-first state persistence (state.json, buildRun, checkpoint/resume), and command-level session segmentation.

**ccproxy, DeepWiki, cc-devflow, CodeBoarding, AntV Infographic, codebase-digest — Progressive visualization, resilient execution, and structured analysis** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-19). Sources: six GitHub repos explored in a batch `/fctry:ref` session. Three cross-cutting themes were identified and five patterns adopted into fctry: (1) hook error isolation — each plugin hook runs independently so one failure never cascades (from ccproxy's error-isolated hook pipeline), adopted into `#rules` (3.3). (2) Progressive section fill in mission control — the full spec structure is visible from the start, with sections transitioning visually as the build brings them to life (from DeepWiki's streaming wiki tree and CodeBoarding's multi-level diagrams), adopted into `#spec-viewer` (2.9). (3) Token-aware project sizing — the State Owner estimates codebase size in context-relevant terms so the Executor can calibrate chunk granularity (from codebase-digest's token counting), adopted into `#execute-flow` (2.7) and `#entities` (3.2). (4) Per-project visual identity — each project in the multi-project viewer gets a distinct accent color for instant orientation when switching projects (from AntV Infographic's seed-based theme generation), adopted into `#spec-viewer` (2.9). (5) Experience-level review analysis — the State Owner reconstructs experience stories from code and compares them to the spec, catching capability drift that structural comparison misses (from cc-devflow's structured review frameworks and codebase-digest's analysis prompt library), adopted into `#review-flow` (2.6).

**Peekaboo — System-wide Observer verification** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-19). Source: https://github.com/steipete/Peekaboo. Peekaboo's macOS-native screen capture and GUI automation via Accessibility APIs — capturing any window at the OS level, detecting UI elements without DOM access, and handling system dialogs programmatically — inspired four patterns adopted into fctry: (1) a system-wide Observer verification tier above the existing browser-only full mode, making any macOS application an observable surface (adopted into `#observability` 6.3), (2) Peekaboo as an external connection with graceful degradation to browser-only when unavailable (adopted into `#external-connections` 3.4), (3) system dialog handling during autonomous builds so blocking dialogs don't stall execution (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7), and (4) application-level and screenshot surface distribution as new observability signals.

**Release Steward + Phase Goals / FPOS — Release intelligence, phase types, and self-improvement** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-19). Sources: `references/ops-steward-agent-idea.md`, `references/phase-goals-fpos-spec.md`. Two concept documents exploring factory extensions. Five patterns adopted into fctry: (1) richer release summary at plan completion — when suggesting a version bump, the Executor now generates a release summary with experience-language headline, user-visible highlights, affected sections, and migration notes (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#details` 2.11). (2) Convergence phases as version arcs — each convergence phase maps to a minor version arc with narrative release notes that tell the experience story (adopted into `#convergence-strategy` 6.2). (3) Executor-inferred phase type — the Executor characterizes each build plan as Capability, Hardening, Refactor, Integration, or Polish based on the readiness distribution, explaining why the plan looks the way it does (adopted into `#rules` 3.3 and `#execute-flow` 2.7). (4) Release summary format — headline, highlights, deltas, and migration notes (adopted into `#details` 2.11). (5) Future self-improvement loop — a `/fctry:reflect` direction that analyzes session friction and proposes system improvements (noted in `#convergence-strategy` 6.2 and `#capabilities` 3.1).

**cord — Chunk context, experience questions, build traces, and behavioral testing** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-20). Source: https://github.com/kimjune01/cord. A coordination protocol for trees of Claude Code agents using SQLite state and typed results. Five patterns adopted into fctry: (1) chunk context model — chunks are either isolated (clean context, no predecessor state) or context-carrying (injected results from completed predecessors), giving the Executor an explicit vocabulary for how context flows through the build graph (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (2) Experience questions as named build state — when a spec ambiguity requires human input, the build enters a formal paused state with the question recorded, blocked chunks identified, and state surfaced in the viewer as a pulsing indicator (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#error-handling` 2.10). (3) Build trace as a first-class entity — a structured per-build artifact recording what actually happened (chunks attempted, retries, context decisions, experience questions asked), enabling post-build analysis and future self-improvement (adopted into `#entities` 3.2). (4) Prescriptive error messages — every error tells the agent or user exactly what to do next, not just what went wrong (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (5) Agent behavioral compliance as an observability signal — tracking whether agents follow declared constraints (token economy, interchange emission, experience language) under specific conditions, catching constraint drift that functional tests miss (adopted into `#observability` 6.3).

**claude-code-cmv — Selective trimming, context composition data, and trimmed transcript fidelity** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-20). Source: https://github.com/CosmoNaught/claude-code-cmv. A CLI tool and TUI dashboard that brings git-like versioning to Claude Code sessions — snapshot, branch, trim, and visualize session trees. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) trimmed transcript as a named context fidelity option — full conversation with tool result bodies stubbed (>500 chars), preserving the reasoning chain and decisions while reclaiming ~50% of token budget, positioned between full transcript and structured summary in the fidelity spectrum (adopted into `#agent-decides` 6.4 and `#entities` 3.2). (2) Empirical context composition baselines — tool results = 60-70% of context, conversation = 10-15%, thinking signatures = 15-20%, system overhead = ~20k tokens constant — validating fctry's context attribution breakdown categories and informing what "healthy" vs "stressed" context looks like (validates `#spec-viewer` 2.9 and `#observability` 6.3). (3) Token economy output taxonomy — explicit named strategies for when each token economy rule applies (stats-extraction for briefings, structure-only for interchange, failure-focus for verdicts), making the existing three rules more actionable for agents (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). Two patterns noted but not adopted: named context checkpoints (relevant to user-facing session management, not autonomous builds) and session export/import (out of scope for plugin architecture).

**rtk — Retrospective context efficiency and filtering taxonomy validation** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-20). Source: https://github.com/rtk-ai/rtk. A Rust CLI proxy that intercepts dev commands and compresses output before it enters context, with 12 named filtering strategies, SQLite-based savings tracking, and retrospective analysis. Two patterns adopted into fctry: (1) retrospective context efficiency in experience reports — after a build completes, the experience report includes a context health summary (whether compaction fired, which sections drove pressure, whether fidelity settings were adequate), following rtk's "retrospective value proof" principle of surfacing efficiency data when the user asks rather than during work (adopted into `#observability` 6.3). (2) Token economy output taxonomy — rtk's 12 named filtering strategies (stats-extraction, failure-focus, structure-only, deduplication) validated and sharpened fctry's token economy rules with explicit context-to-strategy mappings (adopted into `#rules` 3.3, jointly with CMV findings). Three patterns noted but not adopted: transparent hook-based command interception (validates fctry's existing hook-first architecture but no spec change needed), persistent cumulative savings tracking (fctry monitors per-build context, not cross-session ROI), and economic cost mapping (implementation-level concern, not experience-level).

**claude-devtools — Semantic step taxonomy, compaction boundaries, context attribution, event alerting, and tool-specific rendering** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-20). Source: https://github.com/matt1398/claude-devtools. A retrospective session analysis tool for Claude Code that reconstructs session logs into interactive dashboards with context window composition, compaction visualization, and tool inspection. Seven patterns identified, five adopted and two noted: (1) semantic step taxonomy — tool calls within interchange cards are classified as file_read, code_edit, command_exec, search, agent_spawn, or external_tool, with type-appropriate rendering (inline diffs for edits, syntax highlighting for reads, terminal style for commands) (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9 and `#entities` 3.2). (2) Compaction boundary events — when auto-compaction fires during a build, the activity feed shows it as a typed event with build state preservation confirmation (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (3) Named event alerting — important events (retry threshold exceeded, verification failure, context compaction) are pinned with visual accent in the activity feed, surfacing above noise without requiring the user to filter (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (4) Per-chunk context attribution breakdown — the context health indicator expands on hover to show a categorized split (spec content, code, tool output, agent state, conversation) instead of just an aggregate percentage (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9 and `#observability` 6.3). (5) Tool-specific card rendering in interchange — different visual treatments per tool category, driven by semantic step type in the interchange payload (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (6) Incremental append-only build trace parsing — writing trace entries during the build rather than constructing the full trace at completion, enabling live streaming and partial trace reads from interrupted builds (noted as future direction in `#convergence-strategy` 6.2). (7) Waterfall visualization schema — concrete type shape for DAG interchange fields (start time, duration, dependencies, lifecycle state) enabling direct rendering from interchange data (noted in `#entities` 3.2).

**OpenBrowser — Token-efficient browser verification via code-execution architecture** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-22). Source: https://github.com/billy-enrizky/openbrowser-ai/tree/main/plugin. A Claude Code plugin shipping a single `execute_code` MCP tool where the LLM writes Python in a persistent namespace with browser functions, benchmarked at 3-6x fewer tokens than Playwright MCP and Chrome DevTools MCP for equivalent tasks. Two patterns adopted into fctry: (1) token-efficient browser verification — the Observer can use a code-execution browser architecture that returns only extracted data instead of full page snapshots, achieving dramatically lower token cost for verification workflows (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1 and `#external-connections` 3.4 as OpenBrowser MCP). (2) Persistent namespace for multi-step verification — variables survive across tool calls, enabling the Observer to build up verification state across steps (navigate, extract, compare, screenshot) without re-establishing context each time (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). One pattern noted but not adopted: bundled MCP server via `.mcp.json` in the plugin directory — fctry could potentially ship its own browser MCP server to eliminate the dependency on user-installed browser tools, but this is an implementation concern for the Executor to decide.

**skillserver + Agent Skills specification — Ecosystem positioning and plugin format standard** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-22). Sources: https://github.com/mudler/skillserver, https://agentskills.io/specification. The Agent Skills specification (December 2025) is the open standard adopted by Claude Code, Codex, Copilot, Cursor, and 20+ platforms for defining AI agent skills. It specifies a SKILL.md-based directory structure with YAML frontmatter, three-tier progressive disclosure (metadata in frontmatter, instructions in SKILL.md body, resources in subdirectories), and a clear relationship to MCP ("MCP gives agents tools; skills teach agents what to do with them"). fctry's plugin format already conforms to this standard: SKILL.md entry point maps to the skill root, commands/*.md per-command maps to the instruction tier, agents/*.md per-agent maps to deeper instruction content, and references/ on demand maps to the resource tier. skillserver is a centralized skills database implementing this standard with dual interfaces (MCP for agent consumption, HTTP/WebUI for human browsing), representing the emerging infrastructure layer for skill discovery and curation. No patterns were adopted into fctry (the alignment is already structural), but the reference documents fctry's position within a standardized ecosystem and validates two existing design choices: (1) progressive disclosure architecture matches the spec's three-tier model, and (2) the dual-interface pattern (agent-facing and human-facing surfaces for the same content) validates the viewer's bidirectional observation approach.

**Superpowers — Rationalization-resistant instruction design** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-20). Source: https://github.com/obra/superpowers. An agentic skills framework and software development methodology built as a Claude Code plugin, with 14 composable skills enforcing a brainstorm-plan-execute-review workflow. Unlike fctry's non-coder-facing model, Superpowers is developer-facing — but its instruction design methodology applies universally to any system with agent compliance requirements. Four patterns adopted into fctry: (1) TDD cycle for agent instructions — run pressure scenarios without the instruction to observe failure modes (RED), write the instruction addressing those failures (GREEN), close rationalization loopholes the agent uses to bypass the instruction (REFACTOR). This gives fctry a concrete methodology for authoring and hardening the 8 agent instruction files, rather than relying on informal iteration (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (2) Rationalization tables — a reusable format that maps common agent bypass attempts ("This is too simple for the full process," "I need more context first," "The skill is overkill for this case") to specific counter-arguments. When an agent rationalizes skipping a step, the table provides the pre-written response. This sharpens fctry's workflow enforcement from "surface an error when steps are skipped" to "anticipate and counter the specific reasoning patterns that lead to skipping" (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (3) The Description Trap — when a skill or agent description summarizes its workflow, Claude follows the description as a shortcut instead of reading the full instruction content, causing it to skip steps (e.g., doing one review stage instead of two). Descriptions should be trigger-only (what the skill is for and when to invoke it) with no process details. This directly informs fctry's progressive disclosure architecture: SKILL.md descriptions, agent frontmatter descriptions, and command summaries must avoid summarizing workflow steps (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (4) Research-backed persuasion principles for instruction language — authority (framing instructions as institutional policy, not suggestions), commitment (requiring explicit acknowledgment before proceeding), and scarcity (emphasizing what's lost by skipping, not just what's gained by following) as the effective combination for discipline-enforcing instructions (Meincke et al. 2025, N=28k on LLM instruction compliance). This validates and sharpens the tone of fctry's prescriptive error messages and workflow enforcement language (adopted into `#rules` 3.3 and `#observability` 6.3). Three patterns noted but not adopted: two-stage review ordering (spec compliance then code quality — useful for Observer implementation but implementation-level, not experience-level), implementer self-review before external review (minor Observer optimization, not spec-level), and git worktree isolation (explicitly in `#agent-decides` 6.4 scope).

**GitNexus — Spec index staleness, self-guiding responses, precomputed dependencies, fail-open infrastructure** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-25). Source: https://github.com/abhigyanpatwari/GitNexus. A knowledge-graph-powered code intelligence engine that indexes codebases into a graph DB and exposes structural intelligence to AI agents via MCP tools. Four patterns adopted into fctry: (1) quantified spec index staleness tracking — the spec index records which spec version it was built from and includes a prescriptive recovery hint in query responses when stale ("index 3 versions behind, rebuild recommended"), letting agents make informed trust decisions about cached results rather than silently using outdated data (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1 and `#entities` 3.2). (2) Self-guiding tool responses — spec-index queries and Observer verdicts append next-step hints to their results (e.g., "3 unresolved cross-refs — consider loading sections X, Y, Z"), reducing agent reasoning steps in multi-step workflows by leveraging the tool's own structural knowledge (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (3) Precomputed section dependency graph — cross-references and scenario overlap between sections are computed at index time (not query time) and cached in SQLite, giving the Executor a ready-made dependency graph for chunk boundary decisions, dependency edge identification, and cluster detection (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#entities` 3.2). (4) Fail-open principle for infrastructure subsystems — every derived subsystem (spec index, status line, viewer, Observer, hooks) proceeds without blocking when it encounters errors, surfacing degradation as hints rather than hard stops, ensuring the core workflow always works even when every infrastructure subsystem is broken (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). Four patterns noted but not adopted: PreToolUse hook for automatic context injection (validates existing State Owner briefing pattern), global multi-repo registry with lazy connection pooling (validates existing project registry), auto-generated AI context files (validates CLAUDE.md approach), and skill-based progressive disclosure (validates existing progressive disclosure architecture).

**ATM (Agent Team Manager) — Visual agent team management, deployment primer compilation, pipeline chaining** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-26). Source: https://github.com/DatafyingTech/Claude-Agent-Team-Manager. A Tauri v2 desktop application for visual management of Claude Code agent teams via drag-and-drop org-chart canvas. No patterns adopted — all findings confirmatory. Five patterns noted as validating existing fctry approaches: (1) deployment primer compilation (single-doc context bundling for agent execution) validates fctry's State Owner briefing + build plan frontloading, (2) file-based handoff summaries between sequential pipeline steps validate fctry's build trace + state file chunk handoffs, (3) file ownership coordination rule for parallel agent work (distinct files per agent to avoid merge conflicts) reinforces Executor chunk dependency planning, (4) sibling team awareness in deployment primers validates cross-chunk awareness in build plans, (5) sequential pipeline execution with machine-readable status tracking validates buildRun in state.json. Three patterns skipped: typed variable cascade (fctry agents share conversation context, not variable trees), OS-level cron scheduling (future direction, not current priority), and visual canvas as configuration surface (interesting as a two-way spec editing surface rather than a replacement for spec-as-truth — queued as an evolve idea for `#spec-viewer`).

**Dispatch — Background-worker execution, checklist-as-state, IPC with context dump, cognitive load framing** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-25). Source: https://github.com/bassimeledath/dispatch. A Claude Code skill that turns a single session into a lightweight orchestrator by spawning background workers, each with a fresh context window. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) reasoning context preservation on build interruption — when a build is interrupted (session crash, context exhaustion, user closes laptop), the checkpoint now preserves not just structural state (completed chunks, dependency graph position) but also a reasoning context dump — the key decisions, approach rationale, and unresolved considerations from the interrupted chunk — so that resumption starts with richer context than the structural checkpoint alone provides (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#error-handling` 2.10). (2) Background-worker execution as a future evolution path — the Executor may evolve toward spawning fresh context windows per chunk (each worker with a full, uncluttered context) rather than executing all chunks within one session's context window, inverting the context management problem from "manage scarcity" to "create abundance" (noted as future direction in `#execute-flow` 2.7). (3) "Cognitive load transfer" as the value framing for autonomous execution — naming the user benefit as "the factory carries the cognitive load" centers what the user gains (freedom from tracking work, debugging failures, managing context) over what the system does (autonomy), sharpening the pitch for plan-gated execution (noted in `#execute-flow` 2.7). Two patterns noted but not adopted: checklist-as-state where the plan markdown file is both instruction set and progress tracker (fctry's structured JSON state is more powerful for the multi-surface model — viewer, status line, dashboard all read from it — but the legibility of the checklist format is worth studying for build trace files), and multi-model routing per chunk based on complexity (relevant as a future token-efficiency optimization if fctry adopts background workers, but implementation-level for now).

**Zep — Temporal supersession metadata, fused multi-signal ranking with diversity, per-topic digest scope** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-27). Source: https://github.com/getzep/zep. A long-term memory service powered by Graphiti, a temporal knowledge graph engine that stores facts as bi-temporal entities with validity windows, retrieves via multi-signal fusion (semantic + temporal + structural), and maintains entity coherence through LLM-judged deduplication. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) temporal metadata on decision supersession — superseded decision records now carry a `superseded_by` reference linking to the replacement record and a `superseded_at` timestamp, creating a navigable chain so the user or system can trace the full decision history for a given pattern and answer "what was the decision at time T" (adopted into `#entities` 3.2 and `#rules` 3.3). (2) Fused multi-signal ranked selection with diversity penalty — the State Owner's memory injection algorithm now scores entries across alias match, recency, and type priority simultaneously via weighted sum (rather than sequential greedy filtering), with a diversity penalty that diminishes subsequent entries from the same section so no single section dominates the injection window (adopted into `#entities` 3.2 and `#rules` 3.3). (3) Per-topic conversation digest scope — conversation digests are now scoped to topic shifts within a session rather than one digest per session, producing smaller targeted digests (one per section or decision point discussed) that the selection algorithm can pick individually rather than forcing all-or-nothing inclusion of a large session summary (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1 and `#rules` 3.3). Five patterns noted or skipped: LLM-judged deduplication (validates fctry's consolidation pass — 5+ entries about same pattern → cross-project lesson), community detection via graph clustering (requires graph DB, fctry's flat markdown store is intentional), rolling entity summaries (batch consolidation threshold is correct for markdown-first), group-scoped memory isolation (fctry's global store with structural-match gating is the right model), and MMR diversity selection algorithm (adapted as a simpler diminishing-score diversity penalty rather than full MMR, since fctry's entry count is small enough that the simpler approach suffices).

**Trail of Bits claude-code-config — Anti-rationalization Stop hook, credential deny rules, context budget gating** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-27). Source: https://github.com/trailofbits/claude-code-config. An opinionated configuration distribution for standardizing Claude Code across Trail of Bits, a security research firm. Packages global settings, CLAUDE.md templates, hook scripts (PreToolUse blockers, PostToolUse audit logging, Stop hook anti-rationalization), credential deny rules, and slash commands for common workflows. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) anti-rationalization Stop hook — a prompt-based evaluator that detects premature completion signals during autonomous builds ("good enough," "out of scope," "follow-up") and forces continuation. This structural enforcement layer complements fctry's existing instruction-level anti-rationalization design: instructions counter rationalization through persuasion (authority, commitment, scarcity framing), while the Stop hook fires at the decision point and is harder to override through context pressure. Two layers, neither sufficient alone (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#rules` 3.3). (2) Credential deny-rule sandboxing — explicit Read deny rules for sensitive paths (`~/.ssh/**`, `~/.aws/**`, `~/.gnupg/**`, `~/.config/gh/**`, `~/.git-credentials`, `~/.docker/config.json`, `~/Library/Keychains/**`). fctry now recommends these at first run and documents credential safety as a hard constraint, especially important for fctry's non-coder target user who may not understand what the Executor can access during autonomous builds (adopted into `#first-run` 2.1 and `#hard-constraints` 4.4). (3) Context budget gating — explicit threshold (75% context usage) that stops the Executor from starting new chunks, completing the current chunk cleanly and writing a checkpoint for fresh-session resumption. Prevents compaction-degraded builds where later chunks execute with progressively less context fidelity (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). Eight patterns noted as validating existing fctry design: prescriptive PreToolUse blocking hooks (validates prescriptive error convention), context window management guidance (validates pipeline handoffs and progressive disclosure), multi-agent parallel review fanout (validates Observer verification), layered CLAUDE.md distribution (validates three-layer model), self-installing config command (validates dev-link-ensure self-healing), "hooks are structured prompt injection at opportune times" framing (validates hook architecture), statusline with cache hit rate (minor enhancement opportunity), and CI-as-source-of-truth for build discovery (noted but conflicts with agent-decides-implementation). Four patterns skipped: "replace, don't deprecate" philosophy (conflicts with fctry's migration support), package manager enforcement (violates agent authority), audit logging via PostToolUse (build traces are more structured), and telemetry/privacy controls (user's Claude Code settings, not plugin concern).

**semantic-navigator — Sibling-aware labeling, structured intermediate reasoning, semantic neighborhood navigation** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-27). Source: https://github.com/Gabriella439/semantic-navigator. A terminal tool that embeds repository files, clusters them by meaning via self-tuning spectral clustering, recursively subdivides into a browsable hierarchy, and labels each cluster with an LLM using sibling-aware context. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) sibling-aware structured outputs — when agents write or update multiple peer items (scenarios within a feature, sections within a category, claims within a section), they process all siblings in a single structured pass with sibling context, producing more distinctive labels. Each output is written in context of its peers, not independently. The principle: labeling peers together produces better labels than labeling each alone (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (2) Structured intermediate reasoning for concise outputs — when agents produce compressed text (scenario titles, section summaries), the structured schema includes intermediate reasoning fields (`experienceContext` + `distinguishingBehavior` + `title`) that are computed but not persisted. The intermediate fields guide the model's reasoning path toward more precise final outputs (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (3) Semantic neighborhood navigation — the existing embedding infrastructure in the spec index (`section_embeddings` table, cosine similarity) is extended to three surfaces: dependency neighborhood diagrams gain a semantic ring showing embedding-similar sections alongside structural cross-references (visually distinct — dashed edges), the `Cmd+K` search modal gains semantic ranking when embeddings are active, and the State Owner's targeted scans supplement explicit cross-references with top-N semantically similar sections to catch implicit dependencies (adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9 and `#capabilities` 3.1). Five patterns noted as validating existing fctry design: content-hash embedding cache with per-model invalidation (validates `section_embeddings` table), recursive hierarchical depth adaptation (validates recursive kanban), small-repo bypass (validates scan depth scaling), compressed labels (validates status line compactness), and TUI tree filtering (validates viewer fuzzy search). Three patterns skipped: spectral clustering algorithm (fctry's spec hierarchy is declared, not discovered), eigengap heuristic (explicit section count makes auto-grouping unnecessary), and async/semaphore I/O (different runtime model).

**visual-explainer, contrail, value-realization, arifOS, charlotte — Verification depth, learning maturation, interview toolkit, plan framing, and observation efficiency** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-27). Sources: five GitHub repos explored in a batch `/fctry:ref` session. Fourteen patterns adopted across six spec sections, organized by theme: **Verification and observation** — (1) fact-sheet verification checkpoint: the Observer cross-checks structured chunk outputs against source material before committing, catching hallucinated values or misquoted spec text (from visual-explainer, adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (2) Structural diffing: the Observer compares before/after DOM structure rather than pixel screenshots for UI verification, a cheaper and more reliable signal (from charlotte, adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (3) Tiered observation detail: three levels (summary → structural → full DOM), auto-selected by what's being checked so verification tokens scale with question complexity (from charlotte, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). **Learning and memory** — (4) Learning maturation lifecycle: new build lessons start as `candidate` with confidence 1, graduate to `active` after 3 confirmations across sessions, preventing one-off flukes from becoming permanent knowledge (from contrail, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1 and `#entities` 3.2). (5) Confidence scoring: each lesson carries a score that increments on confirmation, decrements on contradiction, and triggers pruning at zero (from contrail, adopted into `#entities` 3.2). (6) Memory authority model: explicit separation between user-authored entries (always win conflicts) and agent-derived entries (can be overridden), preventing the system from gradually overriding user preferences with inferred patterns (from contrail, adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (7) Atomic compaction writes: memory and lesson compaction operations write to temp file then atomic rename, preventing corruption on interruption (from contrail, adopted into `#rules` 3.3). **Viewer and diagrams** — (8) Depth-tiered section content: detail panel renders at three tiers (overview → detail → deep-dive) so users control information density (from visual-explainer, adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (9) Mermaid CSS collision guard: namespaced CSS classes prevent diagram styles from bleeding into viewer layout (from visual-explainer, adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (10) Diagram zoom controls: pan/zoom/reset on complex diagrams, hidden on small ones (from visual-explainer, adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). **Interview and planning** — (11) Value timeline question: "When did this go from interesting to essential?" surfaces the inflection point that reveals what matters most (from value-realization, adopted into `#core-flow` 2.2). (12) Value perception prompt: "Describe this to someone else in one sentence" reveals the user's mental model vs. what the spec captures (from value-realization, adopted into `#core-flow` 2.2). (13) Plan scope framing: minimal/balanced/maximal variants let the user pick scope matching their energy, preventing all-or-nothing plan dynamics (from arifOS, adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (14) State Owner reality index: self-assessed confidence (high/medium/low) in the briefing header so downstream agents can calibrate trust (from arifOS, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). Patterns noted but not adopted: visual-explainer's fact-check slash command (subsumed by Observer verification), visual-explainer's cognitive debt hotspot and understanding gap concepts (interesting for future self-improvement/reflect direction), contrail's DLP lint on memory writes (fctry's memory is local-only, no exfiltration risk), contrail's explicit failure probe strings (implementation-level concern), value-realization's aha moment mapping (the value timeline question captures this), arifOS's tool permission matrix per agent (fctry agents share tool access via Claude Code's permission model), and charlotte as an MCP browser tool recommendation (already covered by OpenBrowser and Rodney/Surf in `#external-connections`).

**Agor — Spatial canvas orchestration, session genealogy, MCP self-awareness, and enriched event streaming** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-27). Source: https://github.com/preset-io/agor. A multiplayer spatial canvas for orchestrating multiple AI coding agents simultaneously, built by the creator of Apache Superset and Airflow. Four patterns adapted and one adopted into fctry across four spec sections: (1) Spatial zone triggers as active decision surfaces — Agor's board regions fire templated prompts when worktrees enter them, making the canvas an active participant in orchestration rather than a passive display. fctry adapts this toward the viewer's kanban evolution: kanban columns and project cards could become active triggers (dragging a project into "Now" could initiate a State Owner scan, moving a section to "Satisfied" could trigger scenario verification) rather than passive priority indicators (noted as future direction in `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (2) Session genealogy with structured callback queuing — parent agents spawn focused children, and completed children queue templated callbacks processed sequentially when the parent is idle, with atomic session patches preventing race conditions. fctry adapts this for the Executor's parallel chunk completion flow: when a chunk completes, its results are queued as a structured callback for the orchestrating session, processed in dependency order when the Executor is ready, preventing interleaved updates from corrupting shared state (noted in `#execute-flow` 2.7). (3) Agent self-introspection via MCP endpoint — agents discover session, worktree, board, and environment state dynamically through MCP tools rather than reading pre-written state files. fctry adopts this as a future direction for the background-worker architecture: when chunks execute as independent workers, each worker queries the orchestrator's live state (completed chunks, current dependency graph, active experience questions) through an MCP endpoint rather than reading a potentially stale state file (noted in `#capabilities` 3.1). (4) Enriched real-time event stream — WebSocket events enriched client-side with context lookups, filtered by allowlist, with an ephemeral buffer and zero performance impact when the panel is closed via conditional subscription. fctry adapts this for mission control: activity feed events can be enriched client-side with spec section context (section title, readiness, claim count) looked up from the spec index, and the conditional subscription pattern ensures the enrichment pipeline runs only when the mission control panel is visible (noted in `#spec-viewer` 2.9). One pattern rejected: multiplayer collaboration (cursors, facepiles, spatial comments) — fctry is single-user by design. One pattern adopted as validation: progressive disclosure architecture (concise top-level map ~560 lines, domain-specific files loaded on demand) independently validates fctry's SKILL.md -> commands/ -> agents/ -> references/ hierarchy.

**compound-engineering-plugin — Model tier selection, structured lesson retrieval, commit heuristics, impact awareness, parity principle, and systematic gap discovery** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-28). Source: https://github.com/EveryInc/compound-engineering-plugin. Every Inc's Claude Code plugin (9,672 stars) implementing a four-phase workflow (Plan, Work, Review, Compound) where each engineering cycle compounds knowledge into a searchable knowledge base. Fundamentally different from fctry (human-AI collaboration at every phase vs. fully autonomous spec-driven development), but its mature patterns translate. Six patterns adopted into fctry: (1) Model tier selection per agent — agents declare preferred model tiers in frontmatter (`model: haiku/sonnet/opus/inherit`), allocating compute capacity where it matters (novel reasoning) and conserving it where it doesn't (structured retrieval). Extends the token economy invariant from output compression to compute allocation (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). (2) Structured lesson metadata with grep-first retrieval — lessons carry structured metadata (component, severity, tags) enabling pattern-match filtering before full content reads, preventing lesson consultation from scaling linearly with lesson count. The learnings-researcher agent pattern (running on Haiku, scanning frontmatter via grep, reading only matching content) directly informs State Owner lesson consultation at scale (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). (3) Incremental commit heuristic — "Can I write a commit message that describes a complete, valuable change? If yes, commit. If the message would be 'WIP', wait." Produces meaningful intermediate checkpoints within chunks (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (4) System-wide impact checklist — five structural questions before each chunk (what fires when this runs, do tests exercise the real chain, can failure leave orphaned state, what other interfaces expose this, do error strategies align) catching integration issues during planning rather than during build (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (5) Parity principle for viewer evolution — from the agent-native architecture framework: anything achievable via CLI should be achievable via the viewer, and vice versa. The viewer evolves toward a full alternative surface, not a read-only dashboard (adopted into `#convergence-strategy` 6.2). (6) Systematic permutation matrix for gap analysis — the spec-flow-analyzer's approach of checking permutations (user state × context × conditions) systematically rather than intuitively, catching edge-case gaps in both review analysis and scenario crafting (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). Four patterns noted but not adopted: parallel multi-agent review roster (fctry's Observer is intentionally lightweight), swarm orchestration via TeammateTool (conflicts with plan-gated execution), cross-platform plugin converter (not a near-term goal), and brainstorm-to-plan traceability with origin linking (interesting but interview state captures this for fctry's model).

**agentchattr — Per-chunk retry limit, cursor-based inbox processing, viewer session security, and dual-interface architecture** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-28). Source: https://github.com/bcurts/agentchattr. A local chat server for real-time coordination between AI coding agents and humans, where agents communicate via @mentions and interact through 8 MCP tools. Fundamentally different coordination model from fctry (real-time chat swarm vs. sequential agent pipeline), but its runtime safety and efficiency patterns translate. Four patterns adopted into fctry: (1) Per-chunk retry limit — agentchattr's per-channel loop guard (configurable max hops, pause when reached, human-reset semantics) adapted as a configurable per-chunk retry ceiling for autonomous builds. When a chunk fails N times (configurable, default 3), the Executor pauses that chunk and continues with independent chunks, resurfacing the failure to the user. This complements the existing anti-rationalization Stop hook (prevents premature completion) and context budget gate (prevents degraded execution) as a third structural enforcement layer — this one prevents infinite retry loops. Per-chunk isolation means one stuck chunk never blocks the build (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7 and `#rules` 3.3). (2) Cursor-based inbox processing — agentchattr's per-agent read cursors (first read returns full context, subsequent reads return only new messages since cursor position) adapted for fctry's async inbox. When processing queued evolve ideas, references, or feature requests, the system tracks a cursor position so agents process only new items rather than re-reading the entire queue. Concrete implementation of fctry's existing delta-first token economy principle (adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). (3) Session token security for viewer control plane — agentchattr generates a random session token per server start, injects it into the HTML page, and requires it on every API/WebSocket call, with origin validation against localhost. fctry notes this as the minimum security model for when the viewer evolves from read-only to input-capable (submit evolve ideas, trigger builds, modify inbox). Low risk while the viewer is passive; essential when it can write (noted as future requirement in `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (4) Dual-interface architecture validation — MCP for agents, WebSocket for browser, server bridges them. Validates fctry's existing bidirectional observation design where agents use API queries and humans use the browser. Three patterns noted but not adopted: multi-agent chat coordination via @mentions (fctry is a sequential pipeline, not a chat swarm), per-agent JSONL queue files (fctry's shared state.json with read-modify-write protocol is correct for the multi-surface model), and activity detection via terminal screen hashing (architecturally infeasible for fctry's plugin model, but the principle of detecting activity from output rather than self-reporting is noted for `#observability` 6.3). Two patterns noted as interesting future references: the "debate" feature (agents collectively discuss a proposed decision — interesting for conflict resolution in spec evolution) and token cost transparency tables (quantifying MCP tool overhead per call — relevant for `#observability` 6.3).

**Batch reference incorporation — Context degradation, codebase indexing, diagram verification, working memory, memory distillation, verifiable artifacts, and error-triggered recall** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-02-28). Sources: 13 GitHub repos and articles explored in a batch `/fctry:ref` session: sharedcontext, deep-research, claude-code-best-practice, Agent-Skills-for-Context-Engineering, srclight, grepai, mcp_excalidraw, macrodata, showboat, claude-mem-lite, claude-code-builder, "The Emerging Harness Engineering Playbook," and creating-agent-teams. Seven patterns adopted across six spec sections, organized by theme: **Context and tooling** — (1) Context degradation taxonomy: naming the four failure modes (lost-in-the-middle, context poisoning, context distraction, context clash) that fctry's token economy rules defend against, strengthening the rationale for existing mitigations (from Agent-Skills-for-Context-Engineering, adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (2) Codebase indexing tool awareness: when codebase indexing MCP servers are available (srclight, grepai), the Executor prefers structured lookups over raw grep for 40-60% orientation token reduction (from srclight + grepai, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). **Memory and learning** — (3) Working memory injection: at session start, the State Owner assembles a working memory snapshot (build progress, recent spec changes, pending inbox items) beyond just lessons recall (from macrodata, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). (4) Memory distillation: after milestones or at lesson density thresholds, the State Owner synthesizes accumulated lessons into higher-order cross-cutting insights that rank above individual lessons (from macrodata, adopted into `#capabilities` 3.1). (5) Error-triggered lesson recall: when the Executor encounters a build error, it automatically searches lessons for related past fixes before attempting its own resolution (from claude-mem-lite, adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). **Verification and diagrams** — (6) Diagram verification loop: when generating diagrams, the agent inspects the rendered result via viewer screenshot or structured observation before finalizing, preventing blind diagram generation (from mcp_excalidraw, adopted into `#spec-viewer` 2.9). (7) Verifiable build artifacts: build traces include executable proof blocks (command + expected output) that can be re-run to confirm reproducibility, turning traces from narrative into machine-verifiable proof (from showboat, adopted into `#observability` 6.3). Eight patterns noted but not adopted: cross-client memory portability (sharedcontext — fctry is Claude Code-only), encrypted memory sync (sharedcontext — local-only by design), iterative deep research (deep-research — different product category), manual compaction at 50% (claude-code-best-practice — fctry's 75% gate is for autonomous builds), episode batching for coherent observations (claude-mem-lite — implementation-level), two-tier dedup (claude-mem-lite — tracked for implementation), dream time autonomous reflection (macrodata — different trust model), and periodic garbage collection agents (harness playbook — beyond current scope). Five patterns skipped: iterative research refinement stages (deep-research), plugin scaffolding (claude-code-builder), hub-and-spoke vs discussion communication modes (creating-agent-teams), planning over execution (harness playbook — already in spec), and unattended parallelization (harness playbook — already in spec). Six references confirmed existing fctry patterns without spec changes: Command→Agent→Skills architecture (claude-code-best-practice), documentation as live infrastructure (harness playbook), strict boundaries make agents more effective (harness playbook), model tier selection per role (creating-agent-teams), security through existing permission model (macrodata), and pop/undo for error recovery (showboat).

**model-matchmaker — Cognitive tier signal, three-tier fidelity taxonomy, single-character bypass** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-03-02). Source: https://github.com/coyvalyss1/model-matchmaker. A Claude Code hook that classifies prompt tasks into model tiers and surfaces a recommendation before execution. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) Cognitive tier signal in build plan — when a plan's heaviest chunk requires architecture-level reasoning, the plan shows a one-line cognitive tier note above the chunk list so the user sees it before approving. Implementation chunks (the default) and mechanical chunks produce no note — silence means expected work. Only architecture-class plans surface the note (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (2) Three-tier taxonomy anchoring context fidelity — the mechanical/implementation/architecture tier classification gives the Executor a concrete anchor for fidelity mode selection within the bounds set by execution priorities: mechanical → fresh start, implementation → structured summary or trimmed transcript, architecture → full or trimmed transcript (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (3) Single-character bypass for non-blocking checks — the `!` prefix convention lets users skip bypass-eligible checks (untracked-change nudges, cognitive tier notes, version validation warnings) without stepping through a numbered menu. The mechanism is documented in the CLI output whenever a bypass-eligible check surfaces (adopted into `#details` 2.11). Mechanism rejected: the reference uses keyword classification to assign model tiers (scanning prompt text for terms like "auth," "database," "refactor"). fctry's no-keyword-heuristics rule applies — the Executor infers cognitive tier from structural signals (spec index metadata, chunk dependency depth, cross-section impact) rather than from keyword matching against prompt text.

**Context+ — Skeleton-first navigation, blast radius tracing, spec coverage orphan detection** (via `/fctry:ref`, 2026-03-02). Source: https://github.com/ForLoopCodes/contextplus. A codebase intelligence MCP server with AST-based structural discovery, semantic code navigation, blast radius tracing, and a typed memory graph with decay scoring. Three patterns adopted into fctry: (1) Skeleton-first codebase navigation as a named Executor discipline — before deciding which files to read, the Executor builds a structural map (function signatures, class definitions, symbol locations) at one of three levels based on codebase size and token budget, then reads only files where the map indicates involvement with the chunk's work (adopted into `#execute-flow` 2.7). (2) Blast radius as a pre-modification check rule — before modifying or removing a shared symbol, the Executor traces all call sites and import sites to determine the change's footprint; broad blast radius changes receive full-transcript fidelity, thorough Observer verification, and a named risk in the build plan (adopted into `#rules` 3.3). (3) Spec coverage orphan detection in the architecture snapshot — files that don't appear under any spec section's implementation footprint are surfaced as spec orphans during `/fctry:review`, as a distinct category separate from drift and unbuilt items, always recommending `/fctry:evolve` (adopted into `#entities` 3.2).
